Well Evaluation
Picture 1. Simmental 2-11 1H location photo. (Jenn Torres, Sunburst wellsite geologist)
1.0) Well Introduction and Location
1.1.1) Well Overview
Zavanna, LLC Simmental 2-11 1H [SW SE Section 35, T154N, R99W] is located approximately
13 miles southeast of Williston in Williams County, ND. The Simmental 2-11 1H is a horizontal
Middle Bakken well within the Williston Basin consisting of one lateral drilled towards the
south. Wellsite geologists will begin logging during vertical hole drilling, just above the Base
Last Salt marker in order to gather data to ensure a curve landing within the desired target. The
curve will be kicked off in the Lodgepole and landed in the Middle Bakken. Seven-inch
intermediate casing will then be set to isolate the target reservoir, after which directional drilling
and geo-steering techniques will be used to maintain maximum exposure to the target zone.
1.2.1) Vertical Offset Wells & Curve Landing Target
· Zavanna, LLC Gust 2-11 1H [Lot 4 Section 2, T153N, R99W] located 0.60 mile west of the
subject well.
· Zavanna, LLC Nelson 3-10 3TFH [Lot 2 Section 3, T153N, R99W] located 1.0 mile west of
the subject well.
· Zavanna, LLC Louise 1-35 H [NWNW Section 35, T154N, R99W] located 0.32 mile
northwest of the subject well.
Figure 1. Map of subject well and correlating offset wells (Source: NDIC website)
The TVD of the landing target, which represents the top of the target zone, was calculated by
assuming comparable formation thicknesses (isopach) between the subject well and offset wells
from the Base Last Salt Marker to the top of the target (Figure 4). As drilling progressed through
the various formation tops and markers, this target was continually monitored and updated as
necessary. A landing target of 11,157' TVD was calculated based off of the Gust 2-11 1H well
and its corresponding Base of Last Salt Marker. The landing target was adjusted to 11,152' TVD
after the False Bakken marker was logged. The curve was landed just below this at a depth of
11,154' TVD and 11,495' MD (Figure 2).
Figure 2. Sidetrack Curve TVD gamma signatures for the Simmental 2-11 1H (Jenn Torres, Sunburst wellsite geologist)
It is important to note the above TVD gamma represents the sidetrack curve landing for the
Simmental 2-11 1H. The sidetrack was necessary due to a loss of the BHA down hole during the
wiper trips after landing the original curve at a measured depth of 11,497', and a TVD of
11,150'.
2.0) Wellsite Geology observations and Geo-steering
2.1.1) Lithology
Lithologic descriptions and sample analysis began in the Charles Formation in order to log the
Base Last Salt for target landing purposes.
The Devonian-Mississippian Bakken Formation is comprised of three members. The Upper and
Lower Bakken members are organic-rich brownish black to black shales. These members are
described as firm pyritic, carbonaceous, petroliferous with earthy, blocky texture. Both the Upper
and Lower Bakken members are believed to have been deposited in a chemically reducing and
anoxic deep marine environment, and are the source rocks for the petroleum system. The Middle
Bakken member has varying lithofacies, and has locally been logged to include the following: 1)
off white to medium gray siltstone located just below the Upper Bakken member 2) off white to
cream lime packstone located just above the ideal target zone 3) off white to tan gray silty
sandstone. The Middle Bakken member is the targeted reservoir for oil production.
2.2.1) Gas Monitoring
This well was lacking a distinct gas trend correlating with stratigraphic location or proximity to
the ideal target zone. There were a total of 5 intervals of noticeably higher gas readings while
drilling the lateral hole (Figure 3). The earliest interval in the lateral was observed from
~12,490'-13,790' MD. Background gas within this interval averaged 1,924 units, with gas shows
ranging from 1,052-4,126 units. The longest segment of the lateral with an elevated gas trend
occurred from ~14,100'-16,620'MD. Background gas within this interval was recorded at 2,767
units, and had gas shows ranging from 2,070-4,977 units. The third interval of high gas occurred
from ~17,680-18,410'MD. Background gas for this interval averaged 2,411 units, with gas
shows ranging from 2,005-5,467 units. It is worth noting the intervals of higher gas could
possibly be due to the formation's structure. The first two intervals occurred while the structure
was steadily gaining in TVD, while the third interval occurred proximal to the height of the
structure.
The shortest interval of higher gas occurred from ~19,180'-19,500'MD. Background gas for this
interval averaged 3,398 units, with gas shows ranging from 2,112-5,075 units. The final interval
of elevated gas levels occurred from ~20,710'-21,575'MD. Background gas averaged 1,950
units, with gas shows ranging from 1,664-6,603 units. It is also worth noting the gas show of
6,603 units was the largest observed during drilling operations and came at a measured depth of
21,074'.

2.2.2) Gas and Oil Shows Within the Vertical and Curve Drilling
The vertical hole of the Simmental 2-11 1H well had a significantly higher background gas than
the other three wells of the pad, averaging 116 units. There were several gas shows reading over
100 units, with the highest gas shows reading over 200 units and are listed as follows: 1) ~56'
below the Bluell top a gas show reading 241 units was observed, and corresponded with a
drilling break. 2) ~182' above the Lodgepole top there was a cluster of gas shows ranging from
209-253 units. Each of these shows also corresponded with drilling breaks. 3) ~10,660'MD there
was a gas show of 214 units within the Lodgepole Formation, just before reaching KOP to build
the curve.
During the curve build the most significant gas shows were observed while drilling the False
Bakken through the Upper Bakken interval. These gas shows were interpreted as a series of
fracture gas shows ranging from 706-2,072 units.
2.3.1) Geo-steering by Gamma Signature
The Middle Bakken of the Simmental 2-11 1H is estimated to be 40' in thickness, with a distinct
low gamma signature from the packstone. The target zone was defined by Sunburst well-site
geologists and the Zavanna prospect geologist as a 4'-thick interval beginning just below the
packstone.
Figure 4. Offset gamma signatures from the Nelson 3-10 2TFH for the Simmental 2-11 1H (Jenn Torres, Sunburst wellsite geologist)
As drilling progressed it became apparent there was a hard streak located at the base of the ideal
target zone. This hard streak coupled with the packstone located above the ideal target zone
resulted in the bit taking severe deflections while drilling within the ideal target zone. It was
subsequently decided to drill just below the ideal target zone under the hard streak. It is also
worth noting the directional component of the MWD tool was not functioning properly for the
majority of the lateral. This presented a unique challenge for geo-steering due to a significant
delay in receiving survey data, causing the steering to be conducted using projection to bit
approximations to determine the attitude of the geologic structure.

Gamma
Figure 5. Cross-sectional interpretation of the Simmental 2-11 1H borehole based on lithology, MWD gamma ray, and ROP (Jenn Torres,
Sunburst wellsite geologist)
Offset wells indicated that the Three Forks structure should drop 20' from curve landing to TD.
However, gamma signatures and sample analysis suggest that the formation had an initial
structural drop of 0.92' (TVD) over the first 592' (MD), yielding a down dip of 0.15°. This is the
second lateral of the pad to yield an initial structural drop. The next interval observed yielded a
structural gain of approximately 28' (TVD) over the next 5,824' (MD) of the lateral. This
yielded an apparent up dip 0.28° for this interval of the well. Over the next 3,611'(MD) of the
lateral, gamma signatures and sample analysis suggest that the formation had a structural drop of
approximately 26' (TVD), yielding an apparent down dip of 0.35° for the second half of the well.
Over the entire 10,100'-long lateral, there was an estimated gain in TVD of 2.4', yielding an
apparent up dip of 0.01°. The Simmental 2-11 1H yielded the least amount of structural drop due
to the end of the well yielding a relatively flat dip compared to the continuous structural drop
observed in the adjacent wells. Geo-steering techniques exposed 33% of the borehole exposure
being within the ideal target zone. The well reached a TD of 21,575' on December 12, 2014.
2.3.2) Geo-steering by Sample Observation
In addition to the general lithology described earlier in this report, it has been observed that the
Middle Bakken member has differing lithologic characteristics depending stratigraphic location
within the formation. The following lithologies (Pictures 2-5) were observed in cutting samples,
and are pictured below in stratigraphic order starting with the siltstone located just below the
contact with the Upper Bakken member.
Picture 2. Simmental 2-11 1H sample from above the lime packstone consisting of off white to medium gray siltstone with dolomitic cement and
subplaty to platy structure. The siltstone was observed to have trace to rare yellow to light brown spotty oil staining. (Jenn Torres, Sunburst
wellsite geologist)
Picture 3&4. Simmental 2-11 1H sample from above ideal target zone consisting of off white to cream colored lime packstone with micro to fine
crystalline texture, and trace to rare yellow to light brown spotty oil staining. There were also trace to common, transparent to frosted loose
quartz grains observed at the base of the packstone. (Jenn Torres, Sunburst wellsite geologist)
Picture 5. Simmental 2-11 3H sample from the ideal target zone, which consists of cream to light gray, very fine grained silty sandstone with
trace to occasional disseminated pyrite, and trace to occasional yellow to medium brown oil-staining. (Jenn Torres, Sunburst wellsite geologist)
3.0) Summary
The Zavanna, LLC Simmental 2-11 1H was spud on July 26, 2014, and reached TD in 42 total
drilling days on December 12, 2014. A sidetrack was drilled after tools were lost down hole, and
the curve was re-drilled beginning at ~10,670'MD. Samples from the Middle Bakken target
indicated an off white to tan silty sandstone with very fine to fine grained, moderate to well
sorted silty sandstone. The oil staining was described as trace to common yellow to medium
brown, and in some cases contained trace visible intergranular porosity. The vertical drilling
revealed a higher than average background gas of 116 units, with 5 significant gas shows reading
over 200 units within the Mission Canyon and Lodgepole Formations. MWD gamma ray
markers, sample analysis, and ROP were successfully utilized to expose 100% of the lateral
borehole to the Middle Bakken, with 33% of the borehole exposed within the ideal target zone.
The Simmental 2-11 1H awaits completion operations to maximize its production potential.
Respectfully submitted,
Jenn Torres
Jenn Torres
Sunburst Consulting, Inc.

Zavanna Simmental 2-11 1H
Lithology
Rig crews and geologists caught lagged samples in 30' intervals from 9,470'- 21,575' (TD), and
in one hour intervals during time drilling from 10,775'-10,082' (MD). All samples were caught
within compliance of North Dakota state regulations as well as the policies and procedures of
Zavanna, LLC. Cuttings were examined wet and dry using a stereo zoom binocular microscope.
Dried samples were then boxed and sent to the North Dakota Geological Survey. All depths are
referenced to driller's depths.
9,470-9,500 DOLOMITIC LIMESTONE: mudstone, light-medium gray, microcrystalline, firm, earthy texture, no visible
porosity; ANHYDRITE: off white-milky white, cream, soft, massive, amorphous
9,500-9,530 SALT: translucent-milky, crystalline, hard, anhedral, crystalline texture; trace DOLOMITIC LIMESTONE:
mudstone, light-medium gray, microcrystalline, firm, earthy texture, no visible porosity
9,530-9,560 SALT: translucent-milky, crystalline, hard, anhedral, crystalline texture
Base Last Salt
9,566' MD, 9,560' TVD (MSL -7,277')
9,560-9,590 DOLOMITE: mudstone, light-medium gray, microcrystalline, very soft, dense, earthy, no visible porosity, no
visible oil stain; trace SALT: milky, crystalline, hard, anhedral, crystalline texture
9,590-9,620 DOLOMITE: mudstone, light-medium gray, brown in part, microcrystalline, soft-firm, dense, earthy texture, no
visible porosity, no visible oil stain; trace ANHYDRITE: cream-milky, soft, massive, amorphous texture
Ratcliffe
9,623' MD, 9,617' TVD (MSL -7,334')
9,620-9,650 ANHYDRITE: cream-milky, soft, massive, amorphous texture
9,650-9,680 ANHYDRITE: cream-milky, soft, massive, amorphous texture; occasional LIMESTONE: mudstone, light-
medium gray, microcrystalline, friable-firm, earthy texture, no visible porosity, no visible oil stain
Midale
9,709' MD, 9,703' TVD (MSL -7,420')
9,680-9,710 LIMESTONE: mudstone, medium gray-dark gray, brown, microcrystalline, soft-firm, dense, earthy texture, no
visible porosity, no visible oil stain; occasional ANHYDRITE: cream-milky, soft, massive, amorphous texture
9,710-9,740 LIMESTONE: mudstone, medium-dark gray, brown in part, microcrystalline, friable-firm, dense, argillaceous in
part, dolomitic in part, earthy texture, no visible porosity, no visible oil stain
9,740-9,770 LIMESTONE: mudstone, medium-dark gray, occasional light gray, brown in part, microcrystalline, friable-firm,
dense, argillaceous in part, dolomitic in part, earthy texture, no visible porosity, no visible oil stain
Mission Canyon
9,781' MD, 9,775' TVD (MSL -7,492')
9,770-9,800 LIMESTONE: mudstone, trace wackestone, light-medium gray brown, occasional cream, microcrystalline,
friable-firm, dense, argillaceous in part, earthy texture, no visible porosity, no visible oil stain
9,800-9,830 LIMESTONE: mudstone, trace wackestone, light-medium gray brown, occasional cream, microcrystalline,
friable-firm, dense, argillaceous in part, earthy texture, no visible porosity, no visible oil stain

microcrystalline-very fine crystalline, friable-firm, dense, argillaceous in part, earthy texture, no visible porosity, no visible
oil stain

earthy-mottled texture, occasional sparry calcite, no visible porosity, trace dead oil stain

Dear Jean:
Pursuant to Commission Order No. 23452, approval to drill the above captioned well is hereby given. The
approval is granted on the condition that all portions of the well bore not isolated by cement, be no closer than
the 200' setback from the north & south boundaries and 500' setback from the east & west boundaries within the
1280 acre spacing unit consisting of Sections 2 & 11 T153N R99W. Tool error is not required pursuant to
order.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: Effective June 1, 2014, a covered leak-proof container (with placard) for
filter sock disposal must be maintained on the well site beginning when the well is spud, and must
remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations are
conducted. In cases where a spacing unit is accessed from an off-site drill pad, an affidavit must be
provided affirming that the surface owner of the multi-well pad agrees to accept burial on their property
of the cuttings generated from drilling the well(s) into an offsite spacing/drilling unit. ZAVANNA LLC
must contact NDIC Field Inspector Jessica Gilkey at 701-770-7340 prior to location construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well
drilling and completion operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will
prevent pollution of the land surface and freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits
are prohibited. All pits shall be inspected by an authorized representative of the director prior to lining and use.
Drill cuttings and solids must be stabilized in a manner approved by the director prior to placement in a cuttings
pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC.
The proposed directional plan is at a legal location. The minimum legal coordinate from the well head at casing
point is: 450' south. Also, based on the azimuth of the proposed lateral the maximum legal coordinates from the
well head are: 10604' south and 1060' east.
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the
approved drilling permit on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to
commence before the 3rd business day following publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may
be waived by the Director. Application for a waiver must be by sworn affidavit providing the information
necessary to evaluate the extenuating circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and any other
information that would allow the Director to conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the
drilling permit, the applicant should retain the permit.
Permit Fee & Notification
Payment was received in the amount of $100 via credit card. It is requested that notification be given
immediately upon the spudding of the well. This information should be relayed to the Oil & Gas Division,
Bismarck, via telephone. The following information must be included: Well name, legal location, permit number,
drilling contractor, company representative, date and time of spudding. Office hours are 8:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m.
and 1:00 p.m. to 5:00 p.m. Central Time. Our telephone number is (701) 328-8020, leave a message if after hours
or on the weekend.
Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey
contractor shall file a certified copy of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion.
Surveys must be submitted as one electronic copy, or in a form approved by the director. However, the director
may require the directional survey to be filed immediately after completion if the survey is needed to conduct the
operation of the director's office in a timely manner. Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one adobe
document, with a certification cover page to certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve
(or when sliding) and 90 feet in the lateral.
Confidential status
Your request for confidential status of all information furnished to the Director, or his representatives, is
hereby granted. Such information, except production runs, shall remain confidential for six months commencing
on the date the well is spud.
Confidential status notwithstanding, the Director and his representatives shall have access to all well
records wherever located. Your company personnel, or any person performing work for your company shall
permit the Director and his representatives to come upon any lease, property, well, or drilling rig operated or
controlled by them, complying with all safety rules, and to inspect the records and operation of such wells and to
have access at all times to any and all records of wells. The Commission's field personnel periodically inspect
producing and drilling wells. Any information regarding such wells shall be made available to them at any time
upon request. The information so obtained by the field personnel shall be maintained in strict confidence and
shall be available only to the Commission and its staff.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12
hours, and tail cement utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi
before drilling the plug or initiating tests.
Logs NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and
porosity zones can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well bore, and
(3) a log from which the presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic cement evaluation
log) in every well in which production or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior to completing the well.
All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as one digital TIFF (tagged image file format) copy and one digital LAS (log
ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a standard CD, DVD, or attached to an email sent to
digitallogs@nd.gov Thank you for your cooperation.

April 9, 2014
RE:
Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Bruce E. Hicks
Assistant Director

1200 17th Street, Ste. 1100
Denver, CO 80202
